  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a528ae48-cf63-4bb4-b571-99407d9ae507'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer8796592373627887969">Sie ist heute sechzehn, kam mit zwölf in einem evangelischen Jugendheim zum Haschisch, mit dreizehn in einer Diskothek zum Heroin. Sie wurde süchtig, ging morgens zur Schule und nachmittags mit ihren ebenfalls heroinabhängigen Freunden auf den Kinderstrich am Bahnhof Zoo, um das Geld für die Droge zu beschaffen. Ihre Mutter bemerkte fast zwei Jahre Iang nichts vom Doppelle</span>
  <span id="freeText8796592373627887969" style="display:none">Sie ist heute sechzehn, kam mit zwölf in einem evangelischen Jugendheim zum Haschisch, mit dreizehn in einer Diskothek zum Heroin. Sie wurde süchtig, ging morgens zur Schule und nachmittags mit ihren ebenfalls heroinabhängigen Freunden auf den Kinderstrich am Bahnhof Zoo, um das Geld für die Droge zu beschaffen. Ihre Mutter bemerkte fast zwei Jahre Iang nichts vom Doppelleben ihrer Tochter. Christiane F. berichtet mit minuziösem Erinnerungsvermögen und rückhaltioser Offenheit über Schicksale von Kindern, die von der Öffentlichkeit erst als Drogentote zur Kenntnis genommen werden. Die Geschichte der Christiane F. wiederholt sich in Berlin, in Kleinstädten und Dörfern bereits zehntausendfach.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8796592373627887969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9749439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9699892301275193988">Living in Rudow and commuting to work through Gropiusstadt, it struck me that I should know the memoir that the neighbourhoods are famous for. <br/><br/>The book, put together from interviews with Christiane F., a teenaged heroin addict, her mother, and authorities working to fight drug use in West Berlin in the 1970s, follows Christiane from her early childhood, when she was abused by her father, who was an alcoholic, to her teenage years, when, desperately hoping for acceptance and love, she sank deeper</span>
  <span id="freeText9699892301275193988" style="display:none">Living in Rudow and commuting to work through Gropiusstadt, it struck me that I should know the memoir that the neighbourhoods are famous for. <br /><br />The book, put together from interviews with Christiane F., a teenaged heroin addict, her mother, and authorities working to fight drug use in West Berlin in the 1970s, follows Christiane from her early childhood, when she was abused by her father, who was an alcoholic, to her teenage years, when, desperately hoping for acceptance and love, she sank deeper and deeper into the club scene around the Ku'damm, with all the associated drug problems. By the time Christiane figured out that addiction doesn't make you cool, she was hooked, selling herself for 40 marks a go at the Bahnhof Zoo to maintain her habit. Christiane doesn't romanticize or preach (which distinguishes this book from others of its kind), but lets her experiences serve as a warning in themselves. Though I found it impossible to sympathise with her, I found the book completely riveting. </span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText11656329206681973977" style="display:none">''We Children from train station Zoo'' were children hooked on heroine in West Berlin during the 70s. They used to 'mingle' on the Zoo station to sell sex to buy heroine. This book is based on a true story of 14 years old Christine F., prostitute and a junkie. <br /><br />As kids, my friends and I were dealing this book like a drug.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2736599830" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2736599830" />
    <a title="Elliot A" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27139785-elliot-a"><img alt="Elliot A" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587678579p2/27139785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2736599830?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elliot A" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elliot A" href="/user/show/27139785-elliot-a">Elliot A</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2736599830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6023873516923689275">I had to prepare a presentation on Bydlowska’s <i>Drunk Mom</i> in my creative non-fiction course and this book (titled <i>Station Zoo</i> in English) was mentioned by the author. I was curious about it, since growing up in Berlin I kept hearing it mentioned, yet I never knew what it was really about.<br/><br/>Whatever somebody could have told me about it would not have been enough to caution me on the journey I was about to embark upon.<br/><br/>The book resonated with me on a very personal note, because part of Christiane F.’s</span>
  <span id="freeText6023873516923689275" style="display:none">I had to prepare a presentation on Bydlowska’s <i>Drunk Mom</i> in my creative non-fiction course and this book (titled <i>Station Zoo</i> in English) was mentioned by the author. I was curious about it, since growing up in Berlin I kept hearing it mentioned, yet I never knew what it was really about.<br /><br />Whatever somebody could have told me about it would not have been enough to caution me on the journey I was about to embark upon.<br /><br />The book resonated with me on a very personal note, because part of Christiane F.’s story took place in Gropiusstadt, a neighbourhood in the district of Neukölln in Berlin; my old neighbourhood. I was born in the hospital just 3 km from my old apartment house; from my bedroom window I could see the roof of one hospital wing.<br /><br />Whenever the narrator mentioned a place in Berlin especially in my old neighbourhood, I knew exactly where she referring to. It gave me an odd sense of nostalgia, but also brought back a lot of the same frustration Christane F. talks about.<br /><br />It reminded me of the endless rules and regulations that made living in Berlin almost unbearable. I don’t mean rules kids have to follow so that they don’t get run over by a car or accidentally put themselves in harm’s way. I mean rules that were applied to the playground, such as the one just downstairs from my apartment. The rules were listed as follows: no playing between 1pm – 4pm, a helmet must be worn at all times, no running, no yelling, no dogs, no bikes, no roller skates, no climbing, no swinging on the swings too high. It was extremely hypocritical, since we found tons of cigarette butts in the sand, along with cat shit; young adults were screaming and laughing until well past midnight and kids were sexually assaulted or having their first sodomizing experience in the bushes that bordered the playground.<br /><br />I understand the narrator’s point that it certainly felt like kids were viewed as the problem, even though they were the victims and just looking for a place to belong.<br /><br />That was exactly what she was trying to do; try and find a place where she felt accepted and belonged.<br /><br />The narrator also went to the same school I went. A school that prided themselves of being one of a kind, yet it failed to properly educate their students. A mentality of competing, of being better than everybody else was nurtured.<br /><br />It was no surprise to see some of my classmates showing up for Latin class smelling like booze and meeting friends of friends that were so high all they could do was shout “moonface” at everyone.<br />The pressure got too much, and all teachers and other grown ups could do was tell them that once they get into the “real world” they are just a number, they should have it better than the previous generation. It is almost hilarious to see how they blindly they spoke and acted.<br /><br />During my research I came across a few newspaper articles that reported on the residents of Gropiusstadt still harbouring sour feelings about Christiane F.’s book giving the neighbourhood a bad reputation. It is curious that <i>Station Zoo</i> is part of the German literature curriculum in high schools throughout Germany, except the schools belonging to the Gropiusstadt school district.<br /><br />Overall, I sympathized with the narrator’s struggles, made me extremely thankful for life I have now. I only wish I had read it sooner. I would definitely recommend it to everyone, although I have yet to find an English copy.<br /><br /><a href="http://www.elliotscribbles.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ElliotScribbles</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6023873516923689275" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_641441931" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/641441931" />
    <a title="Angelica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21280549-angelica"><img alt="Angelica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384923897p2/21280549.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/641441931?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angelica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angelica" href="/user/show/21280549-angelica">Angelica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781936976225" href="/book/show/13435894-zoo-station">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer641441931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15324020200992441008">Having never read a book about any type of addiction before, I have to say this book was pretty hard to read, but in a good way. At times Christiane F.'s story feels like a train wreck, I didn't want to watch but I couldn't tear my eyes away.<br/><br/>I should start off saying that the fact that this story, this girls life, is influenced by drugs so early in life is heart wrenching and at several moments very frustrating. Despite the time gap, it is set in 1970's Berlin, Christiane F. is very descriptive </span>
  <span id="freeText15324020200992441008" style="display:none">Having never read a book about any type of addiction before, I have to say this book was pretty hard to read, but in a good way. At times Christiane F.'s story feels like a train wreck, I didn't want to watch but I couldn't tear my eyes away.<br /><br />I should start off saying that the fact that this story, this girls life, is influenced by drugs so early in life is heart wrenching and at several moments very frustrating. Despite the time gap, it is set in 1970's Berlin, Christiane F. is very descriptive of all the things going on around her and influencing her. I might never visit Germany, but I can most definitely picture Zoo Station, her schools, and the different housing projects she lived in. <br /><br />At times I was drawn in and dragged around Christiane's ups and downs- I understood her need to feel accepted in school, to be part of a group, but I could not and still can't, understand her fascination with local drug addicts. The lure and awe she describes having when she sees in the older kids at school is understandable to a certain extent, with a home life that is less than desirable, her father has huge anger issues and is very abusive to his wife and two children, I wouldn't want to go home either. <br /><br />Christiane F.'s voice is raw, it doesn't apologize or try to make excuses for her turn to her drug addiction, she's honest and blunt, and she doesn't hide anything from readers; which at times is difficult. The translation makes it a little hard to get through at times, but you can see who she is nonetheless. Her battle with heroine addiction is exhausting, taking the reader on a roller coaster of ups and downs, relapses and getting into the mind of someone who really does need constant help to avoid addiction, but can't seem to find it in a place where there is no help for minors, makes you feel desperate for her to find some sort of salvation.<br /><br />If you have a friend or family member who has a drug addiction problem this is a good book to read. It gives you the ability to see and understand what might be going through their mind while they are going through withdraw, relapses and attempting to go to rehab. It might even help you open up a more honest dialogue and finding a resolution. I'm glad I read this book- it helped open my eyes to another world and I think I'm better for it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15324020200992441008" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2097287139" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2097287139" />
    <a title="Tanja Berg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5935491-tanja-berg"><img alt="Tanja Berg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558953813p2/5935491.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2097287139?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tanja Berg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tanja Berg" href="/user/show/5935491-tanja-berg">Tanja Berg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 8203102425" href="/book/show/10662674-v-re-ung-er-for-j-vlig">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5935491-tanja-berg?shelf=biography-memoir">biography-memoir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2097287139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3361385225921066409">I read this book in the original Norwegian 1982 release, recommended and lent me by an acquaintance. It is falling apart. The fragrance of the disintegrating glue had the aroma that book lovers get high on. This book is about other, more harmful highs. I had no idea that it was such a thing until I looked it up on goodreads. Although the events described here are 40 years old, this book is still available in print.<br/><br/>Having now read it, I understand why. It's a rather unique account of the young Ge</span>
  <span id="freeText3361385225921066409" style="display:none">I read this book in the original Norwegian 1982 release, recommended and lent me by an acquaintance. It is falling apart. The fragrance of the disintegrating glue had the aroma that book lovers get high on. This book is about other, more harmful highs. I had no idea that it was such a thing until I looked it up on goodreads. Although the events described here are 40 years old, this book is still available in print.<br /><br />Having now read it, I understand why. It's a rather unique account of the young German drug addict Christiane. How she got into drugs by hanging with the "wrong" crowd that just happened to be her friends. How she went from maruijana to LSD to heroin. How she became a child prostitute to fund her habit. How she tried to get herself out of the addiction, to no avail. Christiane's friends are in the same position.<br /><br />In the middle of the book is a letter found on one Christiane's overdosed junkie friends. In it he writes that he killed himself because - parphrasing - "all junkies cause their friends and families harm. A junkie destroys not just himself, but also other people. That being a drug addict is the worst of fates. So what drives young people into such a mess? Let this be a warning to all those that stand before the choice: shall I try just once? Idiots, just look at me!"<br /><br />The treatment programs available at the end of 1970's were based on adult users. The main premise was voluntary admission. None of the set-up was directed at drug abusers that were still children. The despair of Christiane's mother is shown through her own words, intermittently through the book. <br /><br />This is an eye-opening book, although it shows aspects of life that one would rather not see. Just this morning I read a headline in the paper that the yearly death rate from illegal drugs in the United States is now higher than the number of people killed in traffic. It does not seem that the problem has gotten smaller. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3361385225921066409" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_739035899" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/739035899" />

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3993679-andrea?shelf=sad">sad</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer739035899" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15430942473404227080">Oh, God!<br/>Reading this book was a terrible experience, but I don't regret it. Every kid should read it. <br/>Luckily, I never felt the need to try drugs, and I never knew anybody who used hard drugs. Some of the people I know smoke weed, but as far as I know, that's all. Like I said, I never even tried anything including cigarettes, and I don't plan to. That doesn't mean that I think of myself as a better person than others. I have my reasons for staying clean, and they have their own for doing drugs. </span>
  <span id="freeText15430942473404227080" style="display:none">Oh, God!<br />Reading this book was a terrible experience, but I don't regret it. Every kid should read it. <br />Luckily, I never felt the need to try drugs, and I never knew anybody who used hard drugs. Some of the people I know smoke weed, but as far as I know, that's all. Like I said, I never even tried anything including cigarettes, and I don't plan to. That doesn't mean that I think of myself as a better person than others. I have my reasons for staying clean, and they have their own for doing drugs. I'm not saying that those reasons are valid, but we all cope with our problems differently. <br /><br />Sometimes I wanted to scream at Christiane, sometimes I wanted to hug her etc. But most of all, I wanted to help her and be there for her. I cant blame her for what she did. Not completely. I don't blame her parents either. Yes, they could have done more, but you cant really know what to do in a situation like that. <br /><br />Christiane wanted to get clean, but nobody helped her. Her mother was pretending that everything was normal, her dad was a POS, authorities were turning her away etc. She was just a kid, what was she supposed to do? Nobody helped her! They all turned their heads away. <br />And as much as I would like to help to every person in this world (not just to addicts), I can't. They need to help themselves. But they need support too. Unfortunately, we often react the same way as Christiane's mother, for example. We pretend that we don't see anything. <br /><br />Sadly, things are not much better today. Drugs are still out there, young kids have nobody to guide them...People die from overdosing...<br /></span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review739035899">

<div id="review_1050021575" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1050021575" />
    <a title="Carolina Morales" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14423173-carolina-morales"><img alt="Carolina Morales" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543841140p2/14423173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1050021575?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolina Morales" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolina Morales" href="/user/show/14423173-carolina-morales">Carolina Morales</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1050021575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer146770922882138442">Many people have complained about this book in Goodreads. Nevertheless, I have stumbled into the reason this dramatic report is often disregarded as a valuable novel and it made me appreciate it even more: it is not properly Literature, it's Sociologic/Behaviourist Studies.<br/><br/>I truely appreciate the effort these two journalists have made to try to convert Christiane's true history into a drama novel. But then again, life is not Art and reporters/jounalists are no writers (I'm sorry, but it's true. </span>
  <span id="freeText146770922882138442" style="display:none">Many people have complained about this book in Goodreads. Nevertheless, I have stumbled into the reason this dramatic report is often disregarded as a valuable novel and it made me appreciate it even more: it is not properly Literature, it's Sociologic/Behaviourist Studies.<br /><br />I truely appreciate the effort these two journalists have made to try to convert Christiane's true history into a drama novel. But then again, life is not Art and reporters/jounalists are no writers (I'm sorry, but it's true. <s> Just ask Heminguay and Gellhorn </s> ). The format of the book prevents the readers from any emphatic reaction to Christiane's experiences, as it looks like a copy and paste kind of schoolboard with many pieces of information related to the same theme, all tied to a title and presented together. There are long parts in which Christiane narrates her disease, her desperate craving for the drug, her environment, her 'true' love for Detlef and, of course, her wounded childhood beaten by her father as her mother pretended to look at the other side; there are smaller (and never unimportant) relates of her social welfare assistent, her pshychologist, her mother and even the state attorney who presented a case against her. As stated earlier, it looks like a report, not a novel - and still, it IS a novel, even more, it is a Modern Novel (but I'm not saying it's a particularly good one, mind you). <br /><br />Definition of Modern Novel: a novel in which the main characters are conflicted, divided against her/himselves. The novel must expose closely the environment and society, explain through subtle references the individuals' choices and, MORE IMPORTANTLY, the Modern Novel MUST PLAY with format issues and try to break the straight timeline narrative. Ring a bell, anyone? <br /><br />Back to the novel itself, now. I have been a Junior High student in the 90's and one of the mandatory reads at both 6th and 7th year was Christiane F. The History teacher of my 8th year was fired after putting the Christiane F movie for us to watch during class. What can I say, it was a hit of my pre teen years and all we wanted to be was Christiane F. She was cool, she was free, she was a rebel and, above all, she was AN OUTSIDER. All those who ever found any difficulty in being a round ball often put into a squared hole will identify with this anti-heroine writer(Notice the double meaning, please).<br /><br />However, the path of self destruction leads to...Self destruction. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ All Chrisiane F's friends, possibibly even including Detlef, end up dead by overdosis and she is left alone, a mess of human being, sent to the countryside with her father's mother in hope of a new begining. Has any person who read this really beleived in such an idyllic happy ending? I don't think so.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />Many people advise this novel for teens. It sounds like witch hunt to me - scare them to Hell so we won't have to worry. My advice? Spare the kids, hand it to the parents. Yes, the parents. Parents who cannot cope with frustation, economic trouble and personal bad choices and discharge it to the kids. Mothers who look pretend there is no potential abuser to her daughters. Parents who think, No, my kid is a great child, he's along with friends, not trying to look cool with a weed cigarette on his/her lips. I want to hand a copy of Christiane F's book to all parents of the world and say, Here, you have no idea what your kids may be doing. Here's a hint.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="146770922882138442" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_345722518" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/345722518" />
    <a title="Tiffany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9790621-tiffany"><img alt="Tiffany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338031699p2/9790621.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/345722518?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tiffany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiffany" href="/user/show/9790621-tiffany">Tiffany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer345722518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10677515718118324075">In one of my many adventures (read: rummaging through the books my father brings home), I came across this curious book. <br/><br/>I was 14 and I never knew back then what heroin or drug addiction is. The first few paragraphs were interesting and the character in the book was almost the same age as me so I kept on reading. <br/><br/>It all started with an innocent activity with friends, going to places and meeting new people. I vaguely remember the details but the innocence of the girl resonates. From there, things</span>
  <span id="freeText10677515718118324075" style="display:none">In one of my many adventures (read: rummaging through the books my father brings home), I came across this curious book. <br /><br />I was 14 and I never knew back then what heroin or drug addiction is. The first few paragraphs were interesting and the character in the book was almost the same age as me so I kept on reading. <br /><br />It all started with an innocent activity with friends, going to places and meeting new people. I vaguely remember the details but the innocence of the girl resonates. From there, things went from bad to worse to absolutely tragic, and to think that the girl was so young she could have been playing with friends, watching TV and having celebrity crushes, appreciating music, or just studying. In short, having a normal teenage life. <br /><br />The pages in "H" were like a distorted mirror of myself in some parallel universe--"Christine" went through things that were, for me back then, unheard of. What I love most about this book is that it doesn't glamorize drugs or the lifestyle. It presented things as they were--the cravings, the company she runs around with, her family's discord, the transition from child to junkie. As jarring and eye-opening as it was to a teen life me at that time, the narrative has also been very intimate and honest. <br /><br />In some way, this book has helped prepare me for the life ahead. It provided a preview of a very personal "worst case scenario". There will be nasty things and violence and terrible people in the world. There will be a time you will get hooked in a seemingly unending cycle where there would be no escaping. You may either use people or let other people use you. There will be a lot of vile things all around. Still, our heart of hearts would struggle to transcend. <br /><br />I don't remember how the ending here went but the book, as well as watching "The Basketball Diaries" soon afterwards, taught me one thing: Everyday we go through choices that lead us to different paths. Everything we do, no matter how mundane or harmless it may seem, may lead to a slippery slope from which lives can be ruined. <br /><br />Some people say I'm a control freak but I just don't like to develop bad habits, nor do I condone other people dear to me when they start some themselves.<br /><br />I give this book 3 stars. I will be willing to give it more, that is if I find the book and get to read it again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10677515718118324075" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1506906412" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1506906412" />
    <a title="Alice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48775114-alice"><img alt="Alice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597603562p2/48775114.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1506906412?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alice" href="/user/show/48775114-alice">Alice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48775114-alice?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1506906412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1946361594175414799">Let's start by saying this book is probably the best drug prevention tool ever. As much as it is a brutal read that doesn't save the reader from any of the gruesome details, I firmly believe it should be made a mandatory read in every school and that everyone should force themselves to read every single word. I was never told to read or even recommended this book, I only picked it up when I was planning a weekend in Berlin and thought I would choose something local for the flight. As you can ima</span>
  <span id="freeText1946361594175414799" style="display:none">Let's start by saying this book is probably the best drug prevention tool ever. As much as it is a brutal read that doesn't save the reader from any of the gruesome details, I firmly believe it should be made a mandatory read in every school and that everyone should force themselves to read every single word. I was never told to read or even recommended this book, I only picked it up when I was planning a weekend in Berlin and thought I would choose something local for the flight. As you can imagine, the story of a 14 year old heroin addict might not have been the best first impression of the city, but maybe I don't really regret it...<br /><br />Can you picture that unpleasant feeling that crawls over you when a brand new chalk crayon screeches across a blackboard? That's the feeling this book evokes: the goosebumps, the spine tingling, the eeriness and uneasiness. It's exactly what a candid book on drug addiction should make you feel. Christiane F.'s story resembles a train wreck, you don't want to watch but can't tear your eyes away. Her voice is raw, her words mean and jarring, the sound scratching your eyes which are wide in shock. She isn't trying to make excuses or defend her actions, she's nothing but honest and blunt, with no secrets left to hide. Her battle with heroine addiction is restless and exhausting, giving the reader a tiny glimpse of what pain and desperation she must have gone through. It's frustrating to be the reader, stuck in his role of passively viewing when one would want to step into the book to save the lost youth and change the story, not just of the book but of the lives that were ruined in 1970's Germany.<br /><br />It's a book for thinking about life and Christiane F. is definitely very lucky to still have one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1946361594175414799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_486801852" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/486801852" />
    <a title="Mrs. Kenyon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1639115-mrs-kenyon"><img alt="Mrs. Kenyon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592927206p2/1639115.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/486801852?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mrs. Kenyon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mrs. Kenyon" href="/user/show/1639115-mrs-kenyon">Mrs. Kenyon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781936976225" href="/book/show/13435894-zoo-station">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1639115-mrs-kenyon?shelf=2012-books">2012-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1639115-mrs-kenyon?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer486801852" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3432317071332257224">Six year hold Christiane F. learned many lessons after moving to Berlin. One – there are rules about everything. Two – kids are punished when rules are broken. Three – if you are going to get punished, you mine as well have fun along the way. This philosophy stayed with her into her pre-teen years as she acted out in school and began to hang around with older people. Although the clique was protective of their “baby,” Christiane F. continued to experiment with drugs. She started with hashish and</span>
  <span id="freeText3432317071332257224" style="display:none">Six year hold Christiane F. learned many lessons after moving to Berlin. One – there are rules about everything. Two – kids are punished when rules are broken. Three – if you are going to get punished, you mine as well have fun along the way. This philosophy stayed with her into her pre-teen years as she acted out in school and began to hang around with older people. Although the clique was protective of their “baby,” Christiane F. continued to experiment with drugs. She started with hashish and alcohol, moved on to Valium, Quaaludes and other pills, and was finally addicted to heroin. <br /><br />Zoo Station is a new translation of Christiane F’s tragic memoir about life and drugs in Berlin during the 1970s. Christiane F. was in constant denial about the extent of her addiction and although she could see the effects of heroin on those around her, she continued to believe she could stop at any time. While I had not read the original translation, did not see the movie made in the 1980s and was not familiar with this story at all before reading this book, I was still able to fully experience the drama and tragedy that was Christiane F’s life. The reader will be pulled into the scene with Christiane F. and mourn the loss of her friends and her innocence. Readers of Go Ask Alice will find a satisfying read in Zoo Station. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3432317071332257224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10345181667868681512">Despite its volume this was a very fast read. But it was repetitive, like all addictions are. Ripping off money, shot, going to rehab, repeat. <br/>By the end of it the helplessness of the barely functioning juveniles really got to me. A very vicious circle that a lot of people went through during the heroin epidemic of the 1970's Berlin scene.</span>

<div id="review_2369602502" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2369602502" />
    <a title="Lina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78729919-lina"><img alt="Lina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527769174p2/78729919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2369602502?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lina" href="/user/show/78729919-lina">Lina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781936976225" href="/book/show/13435894-zoo-station">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78729919-lina?shelf=true-story">true-story</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2369602502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15545358200269596656">Usually I have a bit of an aversion to non-fiction works, especially the ones based on true stories. Somehow, knowing that the story is true makes it much scarier and in the same time easier to really get into. And besides, I’m not really a fan of biographical or autobiographical works either.<br/><br/>That is exactly the reason why I, despite hearing a lot of positive things about it and one of my friends literally obsessing over how good it is, was quite reluctant to actually read this book. And at firs</span>
  <span id="freeText15545358200269596656" style="display:none">Usually I have a bit of an aversion to non-fiction works, especially the ones based on true stories. Somehow, knowing that the story is true makes it much scarier and in the same time easier to really get into. And besides, I’m not really a fan of biographical or autobiographical works either.<br /><br />That is exactly the reason why I, despite hearing a lot of positive things about it and one of my friends literally obsessing over how good it is, was quite reluctant to actually read this book. And at first, I thought my suspicions were going to be comfirmed and that this book was really going to be boring, uneventful and altogether bland.<br /><br />But it actually ended up being a lot more than that. It’s really hard to describe what exactly is it about, besides the obvious drugs and addiction, of course. It is a story of people, society, post-WW2 Germany. Friendships being formed and broken. Love. A girl trying to find her place in the world. There is no big reveal, mind-blowing twists or happily ever after, as there is no such things in real life. But it still keeps you interested, makes you feel for Cristiane and her friends more than you ever could for fictional characters. <br /><br />I don’t think this is a book everyone would enjoy. I have struggled with it myself, especially at the beginning. But I still think it’s definitely one worth reading, both for younger people and adults. Even if you don’t really like this type of books, it might still end up exceeding your expectations and making an impression on you.<br /><br />As for me, I went from thinking I’d hate it to actually wanting to watch a movie and maybe even reread it, which I think says a lot. I honestly don’t know why or how I ended up liking it, but here I am, emotionally exhausted, trying to find out what happened to Christiane and Detlef after the events of this book. As I said, it kind of has a way of shocking you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15545358200269596656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1225147597" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1225147597" />
    <a title="Ira Therebel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5902527-ira-therebel"><img alt="Ira Therebel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546421513p2/5902527.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5902527-ira-therebel?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5902527-ira-therebel?shelf=biography-memoirs">biography-memoirs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5902527-ira-therebel?shelf=drugs-addictions">drugs-addictions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5902527-ira-therebel?shelf=western-europe">western-europe</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1225147597" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12190437395502562521">I first read this book in my young teenage years and it had a huge impact on me. It was one of the few books that I have packed when immigrating (not wanting to carry all the weight) and one that stayed on my mind years after I read it. It was what started my fascination with the world of drugs and a big interest in learning more about all aspects of it, as well it was also the book that always kept me from slipping down to a drug addiction where there is no way back from. Real stories like this</span>
  <span id="freeText12190437395502562521" style="display:none">I first read this book in my young teenage years and it had a huge impact on me. It was one of the few books that I have packed when immigrating (not wanting to carry all the weight) and one that stayed on my mind years after I read it. It was what started my fascination with the world of drugs and a big interest in learning more about all aspects of it, as well it was also the book that always kept me from slipping down to a drug addiction where there is no way back from. Real stories like this can do more impact that simple statistics because they show the very raw horror of it.<br /><br />Having read it now as an adult the book seemed even more upsetting for me. Now that Christane and her clique weren't people of my age but the ones whom I saw as children her experience comes even more unbelievable and terrifying to me. We read how young teenagers do drugs, go prostitute themselves because of their addiction, die on overdoses and feel like their life is over and meaningless at the age of 14.<br /><br />The story is told by Christiane herself and we go with her from the time before her addiction but in a difficult childhood to the time it was supposed to be over (unfortunately from what I have read while she is still alive she could never completely beat heroin). We also get to hear from her mother, who I must say should not blame herself for anything. She did all she could to help her daughter with all the little help available. And we also get to read what other people involved got to say about the drug scene at that time (people involved in the police work or drug psychology) and it was indeed very hopeless for somebody who started that young with no help and rehabilitation being designed for that group.<br /><br />Not an easy book to read at all because of how realistic it is, but it is a book that I would recommend to anyone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12190437395502562521" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1632493156" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1632493156" />
    <a title="Jenni" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15878974-jenni"><img alt="Jenni" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356786142p2/15878974.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1632493156?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenni" href="/user/show/15878974-jenni">Jenni</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15878974-jenni?shelf=europe">europe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15878974-jenni?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15878974-jenni?shelf=helmet-lukuhaaste-2016">helmet-lukuhaaste-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15878974-jenni?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15878974-jenni?shelf=history">history</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1632493156" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5191198221285215151">This is one of those books that are incredibly difficult to rate. Because how do you rate a true story that sounds so unbelievable you wouldn't buy it if it were fiction? Because that is exactly how I felt reading this - that if this were fiction, I'd scoff and think the author has gone above and beyond of what is actually possible. But this is not fiction, this is real events and shocking doesn't even begin to describe the contents of this book. Shocking in so many ways - how easy the access to</span>
  <span id="freeText5191198221285215151" style="display:none">This is one of those books that are incredibly difficult to rate. Because how do you rate a true story that sounds so unbelievable you wouldn't buy it if it were fiction? Because that is exactly how I felt reading this - that if this were fiction, I'd scoff and think the author has gone above and beyond of what is actually possible. But this is not fiction, this is real events and shocking doesn't even begin to describe the contents of this book. Shocking in so many ways - how easy the access to hard drugs was in Berlin back in the day, how most of the people mentioned in this book were just kids, how the parents both struggled and neglected their children, how somehow all of this was possible and happened. I don't remember what I did when I was 14, but I can tell I barely knew what heroin was. The kids in this book though, full on addicts, hopeless, very few of them seeing any light or any future. Descriptions of drug use and detox are graphic, and that's part of what makes everything so hard to believe - you keep thinking that a 14-year-old shouldn't know anything about any of this. It's also an interesting reflection on the society back then, and looking back to it almost 40 years later it's fascinating to see how things have changed - but also haven't. The ending of this book is what almost bothers me the most; it's hopeful, but it seems like a dream or something made up as well. <br /><br />I understand very well why schools have made this a mandatory read - I think everyone should pick this up and force themselves to read every single word in this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5191198221285215151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_1249630'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1249630.Os_Maias?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Os Maias<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/6913270.E_a_de_Queir_s?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Eça de Queirós<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.02 avg rating &mdash; 17,224 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1888\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer5531002404698372020\">Biblioteca Ulisseia de Autores Portugueses #15\n\nOs Maias é uma das obras mais conhecidas do escritor português Eça de Queiroz. O livro foi publicado no Porto em 1888. A acção de Os Maias passa-se em Lisboa, na segunda metade do século XIX, e apresent<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText5531002404698372020\" style=\"display:none\">Biblioteca Ulisseia de Autores Portugueses #15\n\nOs Maias é uma das obras mais conhecidas do escritor português Eça de Queiroz. O livro foi publicado no Porto em 1888. A acção de Os Maias passa-se em Lisboa, na segunda metade do século XIX, e apresenta-nos a história de três gerações da família Maia. A acção inicia-se no Outono de 1875, quando Afonso da Maia, nobre e pobre proprietário, se instala no Ramalhete com o neto recém formado em Medicina. Neste momento faz-se uma longa descrição da casa - &quot;O Ramalhete,&quot; cujo nome tem origem num painel de azulejos com um ramo de girassóis, e não em algo fresco ou campestre, tal como o nome nos remete a pensar. Afonso da Maia era o personagem mais simpático do romance e aquele que o autor mais valorizou, pois não se lhe conhecem defeitos. É um homem de carácter, culto e requintado nos gostos. Em jovem aderiu aos ideais do Liberalismo e foi obrigado, por seu pai, a sair de casa e a instalar-se em Inglaterra. Após o pai falecer regressa a Lisboa para casar com Maria Eduarda Runa, mas pouco tempo depois escolhe o exílio por razões de ordem política. Há em Os Maias um retrato da Lisboa da epóca. Carlos, que mora na Rua das Janelas Verdes, caminha com frequência até ao Rossio (embora, por vezes, vá a cavalo ou de carruagem). Algumas das lojas citadas no livro ainda existem - a Casa Havaneza, no Chiado, por exemplo. É possível seguir os diferentes percursos de Carlos ou do Ega pelas suas da Baixa lisboeta, ainda que algumas tenham mudado de nome. No final do livro, quando Carlos volta a Lisboa muitos anos depois, somos levados a ver as novidades - a Avenida da Liberdade, que substituiu o Passeio Público, e que é descrita como uma coisa nova, e feia pela sua novidade, exactamente como nos anos 70 se falava das casas de emigrante. O romance veicula sobre o país uma perspectiva muito derrotista, muito pessimista. Tirando a natureza (o Tejo, Sintra, Santa Olávia...), é tudo uma choldra ignóbil. Predomina uma visão de estrangeirado, de quem só valoriza as civilizações superiores - da França e Inglaterra, principalmente. Os políticos são mesquinhos, ignorantes ou corruptos (Gouvarinho, Sousa Neto...); os homens das Letras sao boémios e dissolutos, retrógrados ou distantes da realidade concreta (Alencar, Ega...: lembre-se o que se passou no Sarau do Teatro da Trindade); os jornalistas boémios e venais (Palma...); os homens do desporto não conseguem organizar uma corrida de cavalos, pois não há hipódromo à altura, nem cavalos, nem cavaleiros, as pessoas não vestem como o evento exigia, as senhoras traziam vestidos de missa. Para cúmulo de tudo isto, os protagonistas acabam vencidos da vida. Apesar de ser isto referido no fim do livro, pode-se ver que ainda há alguma esperanca implícita, nas passagens em que Carlos da Maia e João da Ega dizem que o apetite humano é a causa de todos os seus problemas e que portanto nunca mais terão apetites, mas logo a seguir dizem que lhes está a apetecer um &quot;prato de paio com ervilhas,&quot; ou quando dizem que a pressa não leva a nada e que a vida deve ser levada com calma mas começam a correr para apanhar o americano (eléctrico). Mais do que crítica de costumes, o romance mostra-nos um país - sobretudo Lisboa - que se dissolve, incapaz de se regenerar. Quando o autor escreve mais tarde A Cidade e as Serras, expõe uma atitude muito mais construtiva: o protagonista regenera-se pela descoberta das raízes rurais ancestrais não atingidas pela degradação da civilização, num movimento inverso ao que predomina n\'Os Maias.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"5531002404698372020\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n I due però non hanno in comune il sangue, ma qualcosa di più profondo. A legarli è un’amicizia ruvida come l’intonaco sbrecciato dei palazzi in cui abitano, nata quando erano bambini e sopravvissuta a tutto ciò che di oscuro la vita può regalare. Un’amicizia che cresce con loro fino a diventare un amore selvaggio, graffiante come vetro spezzato, delicato e luminoso come un girasole. Un amore nato nonostante tutto e tutti, nonostante loro stessi per primi.\nMa alle soglie dei vent’anni, la voce di Beatrice è stanca e strozzata. E il cuore fragile di Alfredo ha perso i suoi colori. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10667491735251525993">DE: Vera Christiane Felscherinow wurde als jugendliche Drogenabhängige zu einer Symbolfigur für die Verbreitung des Drogenmissbrauchs in Deutschland und der damit verbundenen Probleme in der deutschen Gesellschaft. Bekannt wurde sie in der Öffentlichkeit gegen Ende der 1970er-Jahre durch eine Reportage und ein begleitendes Buch der Zeitschrift Stern unter der abgekürzten Namensform „Christiane F.“</span>
  <span id="freeText10667491735251525993" style="display:none">DE: Vera Christiane Felscherinow wurde als jugendliche Drogenabhängige zu einer Symbolfigur für die Verbreitung des Drogenmissbrauchs in Deutschland und der damit verbundenen Probleme in der deutschen Gesellschaft. Bekannt wurde sie in der Öffentlichkeit gegen Ende der 1970er-Jahre durch eine Reportage und ein begleitendes Buch der Zeitschrift Stern unter der abgekürzten Namensform „Christiane F.“ Sie hatte eine Karriere als Sängerin unter dem Namen Sentimentale Jugend.<br /><br />EN: Christiane F. (born Vera Christiane Felscherinow) is a former heroin addict famous for her autobiographical book Wir Kinder vom Bahnhof Zoo which describes her struggle with drug addiction during her teens. She went on to have a singing career.<br /><br />See <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14124419.Christiane_V__Felscherinow" title="Christiane V. Felscherinow" rel="nofollow noopener">Christiane V. Felscherinow</a></span>
